  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_34e82aac-4459-44d6-b738-1a791f963113'
      });
    }

<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_1485135'><a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F16124019-waking-up-married">like</a></span>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/91258850-drew-jaden"><img alt="" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_100x100-259587f1619f5253426a4fa6fb508831.png" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/91258850-drew-jaden">Drew Jaden</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I was experiencing a gradual rejection from my girlfriend, I couldn’t tell if she was loving or hating me. After 1 and half year together we decided t<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I was experiencing a gradual rejection from my girlfriend, I couldn’t tell if she was loving or hating me. After 1 and half year together we decided to make our dream come through by moving in together, 3 days before moving she changed her mind and became super angry, she spoked foul language and didn’t accept any hug, kiss or even conversation. She turned against me within minutes and said she hates me and am the worst thing that ever happened to her, she said that I destroyed her dreams. She totally forgot when she told me that I am the man of her life and she wanna grow old with me. I missed the wave to love or let go because of fear of starting all over and finding the perfect woman. Her friends whom I don’t personally know called me a cheat since she spoke bad about me to them.<br />I reached out for love union spell from Dr. Wakina via his email dr.wakinalovetemple@gmail.comI was told by Doc that her best friend cast a magic spell on us. Dc Wakina told me it’s not too late to bring her back and I will be granted another opportunity to make our dream come true.<br />We were finally established to blossom our best qualities with each other, perfect communication, understanding and respect was also restored as we now live together as life partner, lover and friends. I wouldn’t have recovered all without a love and peaceful spell done by Dr. Wakina. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

<div id="review_489064795" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/489064795" />
    <a title="Rebekah Weatherspoon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4754166-rebekah-weatherspoon"><img alt="Rebekah Weatherspoon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1345864493p2/4754166.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/489064795?book_show_action=true">Dec 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebekah Weatherspoon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebekah Weatherspoon" href="/user/show/4754166-rebekah-weatherspoon">Rebekah Weatherspoon</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4754166-rebekah-weatherspoon?shelf=whaaaaaa">whaaaaaa</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer489064795" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10832924489084943106">short: this should have been called "You In Danger, Girl".<br/><br/>long: i was totally in the mood for something light and a little cheesy and fun. i love cheesy rom coms. something with a title like Waking Up Married is usually right up my alley. I THOUGHT! this story would go something like this:<br/><br/>woman wakes up married to a guy she met in vegas. <br/>they know they need to break up.<br/>he woooooooos her.<br/>it's super corny.<br/>it's super cute.<br/>there's a montage.<br/>they realize they are meant to be together.<br/>they kiss.<br/>the en</span>
  <span id="freeText10832924489084943106" style="display:none">short: this should have been called "You In Danger, Girl".<br /><br />long: i was totally in the mood for something light and a little cheesy and fun. i love cheesy rom coms. something with a title like Waking Up Married is usually right up my alley. I THOUGHT! this story would go something like this:<br /><br />woman wakes up married to a guy she met in vegas. <br />they know they need to break up.<br />he woooooooos her.<br />it's super corny.<br />it's super cute.<br />there's a montage.<br />they realize they are meant to be together.<br />they kiss.<br />the end.<br /><br />THAT DIDN'T HAPPEN.<br /><br />in a nutshell, they get married. Megan wants to break it off because who wouldn't after marrying a stranger after being black out drunk, but oh no. Connor is not having that. he spends the entire book trying to force her to stay with him because they both want a family. and because he think she's hot. i understand the idea of a marriage of convenience, but to be honest Connor was just scary. every time he opened his mouth he said something manipulative and controlling. <br /><br />Megan who is super independent and smart and seriously doesnt need this dude AT ALL, fights him every time, but then caves seconds later for no reason other than the fact that he was hot? or had money and sperm she didn't need? he deliberately goes against her wishes more than once. he refuses to agree to very simple requests and then he goes nuts when she disobeys him. i am over emotionally abusive heroes. for reals.<br /><br />my other issue as with the writing itself. each scene seemed to be wordy with very little action. Connor thinks the same things over and over. also describing him as being "traditionally" handsome with traditional good looks rubbed me irky. as did the whole page where Megan reasons that he must be gay, because there's no way a man that attractive would want to be with her to have a baby. in 2013, hot, white, rich gay men have very little trouble acquiring babies. sorry. <br /><br />i really wanted to love this this book, but i found myself gritting my teeth and shaking my fist in the air all the way to the end.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10832924489084943106" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_468047882" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/468047882" />
    <a title="Katy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4572741-katy"><img alt="Katy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1365039295p2/4572741.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/468047882?book_show_action=true">Dec 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katy" href="/user/show/4572741-katy">Katy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer468047882" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8891548089588358907">Yes, I do know this book is very predictable, and I do know that it's probably not very realistic because a guy like that really doesn't exist. But I don't care. I loved this book anyway.<br/><br/>Why? Because of the dialogue. That was the thing that won me over about this book. Kelly had a knack for writing some really good lines that had me grin like a fool, laugh out loud, and even for one tiny moment, make my eyes misty.<br/><br/>I mean, I'm reading a Harlequin romance. How complicated can it be. And there are </span>
  <span id="freeText8891548089588358907" style="display:none">Yes, I do know this book is very predictable, and I do know that it's probably not very realistic because a guy like that really doesn't exist. But I don't care. I loved this book anyway.<br /><br />Why? Because of the dialogue. That was the thing that won me over about this book. Kelly had a knack for writing some really good lines that had me grin like a fool, laugh out loud, and even for one tiny moment, make my eyes misty.<br /><br />I mean, I'm reading a Harlequin romance. How complicated can it be. And there are so many Harlequinn and similar type of romantic comedies that you will run into those with the same story line. But what set this book apart was the writing.<br /><br />MEMORABLE (EDITED) SCENES: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br /><br />“Man, I love it when you get my name right.”<br /><br />“You got married,” she gasped. “At my wedding?”<br />“No, of course not,” he assured with all the sensitivity of an assassin. “We got married first. This morning.<br /><br />“Yeah, but what’s in it for you?”<br />“Ten minutes to convince you to give me twenty."<br /><br />“Of all the stupid, self-sabotaging, dangerous—”<br />“Megan.”<br />What had she done? Even if she wasn’t pregnant, she’d had unprotected sex with a man she didn’t know. ...patient zero...<br />Her stomach pitched hard. “He could have an STD,” she gasped, her own anxiety pushing the words past her lips before she’d thought to stifle them.<br />“Megan.” This time her name sounded strained coming through his lips. As though this guy was losing his patience.<br />Tough. Whatever he was thinking, he’d have to put a pin in it.<br />“Damn it, Megan, look at me.” <br />(Connor lists 1-5.)<br />So he was gay.<br /><br />9:02 p.m....JEFF: WAIT 4 ME<br />9:04 p.m....JEFF: PICK UP YOUR PHONE<br />9:57 p.m....JEFF: You should stop for drink @ that bar in terminal with the big olives B4 flight<br />10:22 p.m....REED: Hey, UR at the bar. You look pissed <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Both Megan and Connor are certifiably crazy - incredibly frustrating but at the same time charming. And Connor is too good to be true. He knew exactly what to say. And even when he didn't, his imperfections and flaws were also attractive. How did Kelly do that?!?<br /><br />Like I said, it's not hard to guess what will happen. And I'm a sucker for cute, fun reads anyway. With this book, it was just a really entertaining experience to read such a delightful book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8891548089588358907" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_501435034" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/501435034" />
    <a title="Jill" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3820197-jill"><img alt="Jill" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1383385041p2/3820197.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/501435034?book_show_action=true">Jan 09, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jill" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jill" href="/user/show/3820197-jill">Jill</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Jill by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/4299312">...</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3820197-jill?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer501435034" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2952358382802132150"><br/><br/>Megan Scott in Las Vegas for her cousin's wedding, wakes up after a night out on the town with a handsome stranger, to find herself married. Connor Reed is surprised that he and Megan click so well even after just one night. He's so happy about the arrangement, he'd like to make the marriage permanent. Trying to talk Megan out of a divorce though is going to be tough.<br/><br/>So the story line isn't exactly new. If you've seen the movie <i>What Happens in Vegas</i> you'll know what I mean. But the execution is </span>
  <span id="freeText2952358382802132150" style="display:none"><br /><br />Megan Scott in Las Vegas for her cousin's wedding, wakes up after a night out on the town with a handsome stranger, to find herself married. Connor Reed is surprised that he and Megan click so well even after just one night. He's so happy about the arrangement, he'd like to make the marriage permanent. Trying to talk Megan out of a divorce though is going to be tough.<br /><br />So the story line isn't exactly new. If you've seen the movie <i>What Happens in Vegas</i> you'll know what I mean. But the execution is really well done. It's well-written, it's fun and the romance develops believably (well as much as can be expected in fiction...). Both Connor (especially!) and Megan are likable leads.<br /><br />The first part of the story is light-hearted and just fun. Later in the second half a bit of angst develops with some conflict between the protags, but it adds to the story and of course it all works out. <br /><br />I enjoyed this a lot. Well worth picking up if you like light, cute contemporary romances.<br /><br /><b>Steam:</b> 2.5-3<br /><br /><i>* Thanks Bri for the recommendation</i><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2952358382802132150" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/490245451?book_show_action=true">Dec 30, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katrina Passick Lumsden" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katrina Passick Lumsden" href="/user/show/1964146-katrina-passick-lumsden">Katrina Passick Lumsden</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer490245451" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8530618523512381254">This is one of those books that makes you throw up in your mouth multiple times, and you can't figure out why you're still reading it after the first chapter...until you realize you've nothing better to do, it's a quick and easy way to add another book to your tally for the year, and oh yeah, you're a complete masochist. <br/><br/>I knew I was in trouble after reading the first couple of pages, during which I was assaulted with one adjective-riddled, anecdotal cliche after another. Anything that is suppos</span>
  <span id="freeText8530618523512381254" style="display:none">This is one of those books that makes you throw up in your mouth multiple times, and you can't figure out why you're still reading it after the first chapter...until you realize you've nothing better to do, it's a quick and easy way to add another book to your tally for the year, and oh yeah, you're a complete masochist. <br /><br />I knew I was in trouble after reading the first couple of pages, during which I was assaulted with one adjective-riddled, anecdotal cliche after another. Anything that is supposed to be funny falls embarrassingly flat, neither character is likable in any way whatsoever, the story is tired, the plot devices weak and, I'm sorry, I am sick to death of reading shit like this; <b>
  <i>"This guy and all his good looks weren't a part of her plan. So what if he was handsome, or that she'd seen hints of the kind of humor she typically appreciated, or that she was, in fact, married to him? She'd had enough close calls in her life with the men she'd actually <u>known</u>, and she was through with the whole business."</i>
</b><br /><br />That was the <i>fifth page</i>. Nothing quite like being subtle and leading your readers quietly around to the intricate workings of your characters. Nah, fuck that, let's just shove it all in their faces right out of the gate so that they have the <i>entire fucking book</i> to digest the fact that wonder heroine with the heart of a sadistic cyborg and the mind of an inebriated chimp <u>has a plan</u>. Seriously, I couldn't have figured it out without the author jamming it down my gullet like that, so I appreciate the candor. <br /><br />On top of the terrible writing, the characterization is just sickening. Emotionally stunted Megan, in an attempt to prove emotionally stunted Connor will just end up leaving her, devises a plan to make him see how completely and totally undesirable she is as a partner by doing things like....making bad food and wearing a stinky face mask around the house. Like I said, the mind of an inebriated chimp. <br /><br />Typical HEA ending, as well, one you could see coming 10,000 miles away. I'm OK with that most of the time, but on top of everything else, it was just another disappointment. And the whole thing was so...<b>sappy!</b> Just. No. If you seek an engaging romantic read, look elsewhere, this story is barren, bereft, and bewildering.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8530618523512381254" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17246809337346354586">My first try at the new Harlequin Kiss line. My second read by this author. I liked this book. It felt fresh and modern. It was one of those books where the story revolved solely around the hero and heroine's feelings and relationship. There was almost no description. Once the ocean was mentioned and some floor to ceiling windows but that was about it. There were a total of 5 scenes that included other people and they were extremely brief and the other characters were not important and were left</span>
  <span id="freeText17246809337346354586" style="display:none">My first try at the new Harlequin Kiss line. My second read by this author. I liked this book. It felt fresh and modern. It was one of those books where the story revolved solely around the hero and heroine's feelings and relationship. There was almost no description. Once the ocean was mentioned and some floor to ceiling windows but that was about it. There were a total of 5 scenes that included other people and they were extremely brief and the other characters were not important and were left totally undescribed. The one secondary character who seemed to be somewhat important, the hero's best friend, was never in any scene with both the hero and the heroine. that seemed a missing scene to me. I don't think he ever met her. There was a lot of telling to get to the next showing part and quite a bit of introspection, especially on the hero's part. It all seemed part of the author's style though so it didn't bother me too much.<br /><br />On the whole an appealing book.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer467033394" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer17992167670895444774"><b>3 stars</b><br/><br/>You all have heard that saying: "What happens in Vegas, stays in Vegas." Now, in some cases that would (kind of) be true - denial is a true life-saver at times, but some things simply can't be pushed under the carpet.<br/><blockquote>
  <span>[image error]</span>
</blockquote><br/>Take Megan, for instance. The morning after her cousin's bachelorette party, she wakes up in a stranger's bed, and she's wearing a wedding ring! <br/><blockquote>
  <span>[image error]</span>
</blockquote><br/>Now if only she could remember how exactly did she ended up there, all would be all right.<br/><br/>For his</span>
  <span id="freeText17992167670895444774" style="display:none"><b>3 stars</b><br><br>You all have heard that saying: "What happens in Vegas, stays in Vegas." Now, in some cases that would (kind of) be true - denial is a true life-saver at times, but some things simply can't be pushed under the carpet.<br><blockquote>
  <span>[image error]</span>
</blockquote><br>Take Megan, for instance. The morning after her cousin's bachelorette party, she wakes up in a stranger's bed, and she's wearing a wedding ring! <br><blockquote>
  <span>[image error]</span>
</blockquote><br>Now if only she could remember how exactly did she ended up there, all would be all right.<br><br>For his part, Connor is surprisingly pleased by the turn of events. He wants to settle down and have a family, it's just that he hasn't been lucky so far. But after he got to know Megan he realized that she is perfect for him. Now, all he has to do is to convince her of that.<br><br>A likable story about two people learning that loves takes no prisoners.<br><br>The plot is engaging and interesting. The fact that the hero is the one who wants to stay married, who is pursuing the heroine, trying to convince her that marriage is a great thing is truly refreshing. <br><br>I enjoyed the first half of the book. While Megan was a trifle annoying with trying to sabotage the marriage, Connor made for it. And then he was the one who went cold on her overnight. And that negatively impacted my enjoyment of the book. I dislike character who have major attitude changes, and Connor was truly a shinning example of the type.<br><br>I'm truly intrigued by this new Harlequin series. It sounds as if it will be really enjoyable.<br><br>For those interested, this book is free at both amazon and eHarlequin (and probably other retailers, but I can't guarantee it).<br><br><i>ARC provided by Harlequin via NetGalley</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="17992167670895444774" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_451044699" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/451044699" />
    <a title="Suzie Quint" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4979877-suzie-quint"><img alt="Suzie Quint" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442600629p2/4979877.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/451044699?book_show_action=true">Nov 07, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Suzie Quint" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Suzie Quint" href="/user/show/4979877-suzie-quint">Suzie Quint</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4979877-suzie-quint?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4979877-suzie-quint?shelf=kindle-loanable">kindle-loanable</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer451044699" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6907909597339845260">There are some tropes that are fun but hard to write without having them seem contrived. The accidental marriage is one of them, but Ms Kelly pulls it off nicely. <br/><br/>Neither of them is looking for love. He wants a marriage that based on liking, shared goals and values without the mess of strong emotions. She's given up on relationships but wants children and has plans to get artificially inseminated. When they meet in Vegas and have a gloriously fun night, he decides she's everything he's looking f</span>
  <span id="freeText6907909597339845260" style="display:none">There are some tropes that are fun but hard to write without having them seem contrived. The accidental marriage is one of them, but Ms Kelly pulls it off nicely. <br /><br />Neither of them is looking for love. He wants a marriage that based on liking, shared goals and values without the mess of strong emotions. She's given up on relationships but wants children and has plans to get artificially inseminated. When they meet in Vegas and have a gloriously fun night, he decides she's everything he's looking for and talks her into getting married, not realizing that she's drunk enough that she'll remembers little the next morning. Convincing the heroine to give them a chance could have been a disaster in the hands of an impatient author, but Ms. Kelly gets there in a nicely paced, methodical, and logical fashion, creating realistic reasons for her to agree. Not once did I roll my eyes. (A common event when I'm asked to stretch credibility too far.)<br /><br />Since I bought into the set up, I was able to relax and enjoy the way the story played out. I do like when the hero is confident enough to put himself out there and go after the woman he wants, and Ms. Kelly writes such men well so this is another winner.<br /><br />My favorite part? How, in the beginning, she can't get his name right.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6907909597339845260" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2390207438" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2390207438" />
    <a title="Caz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4368838-caz"><img alt="Caz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1332962126p2/4368838.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2390207438?book_show_action=true">May 15, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Caz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Caz" href="/user/show/4368838-caz">Caz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4368838-caz?shelf=fluff">fluff</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4368838-caz?shelf=aar">aar</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4368838-caz?shelf=romance-other">romance-other</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4368838-caz?shelf=2018-tbr-challenge">2018-tbr-challenge</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2390207438" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14845581048496453209"><b>I've given this a C+ -3.5 stars</b><br/><br/>Scrolling through my Kindle to find a contemporary romance to read for this month’s prompt, I stumbled upon Mira Lyn Kelly’s <strong>Waking Up Married</strong>, one of the titles in Harlequin’s short-lived <strong>
  <em>Kiss </em>
</strong>line (which is published as <strong>
  <em>Mills & Boon Modern Tempted</em>
</strong> in the UK).  I’ve read a couple of the author’s more recent titles and enjoyed them – funny, sexy and sweet, they’re written with a secure but deft hand and boast attractive principals and a strong supporting ca</span>
  <span id="freeText14845581048496453209" style="display:none"><b>I've given this a C+ -3.5 stars</b><br /><br />Scrolling through my Kindle to find a contemporary romance to read for this month’s prompt, I stumbled upon Mira Lyn Kelly’s <strong>Waking Up Married</strong>, one of the titles in Harlequin’s short-lived <strong>
  <em>Kiss </em>
</strong>line (which is published as <strong>
  <em>Mills &amp; Boon Modern Tempted</em>
</strong> in the UK).  I’ve read a couple of the author’s more recent titles and enjoyed them – funny, sexy and sweet, they’re written with a secure but deft hand and boast attractive principals and a strong supporting cast.  I went into this one hoping for more of the same and found it, for the most part, but the story as a whole is rather let down by the hero who spends most of the novel trying to persuade the heroine into doing something she isn’t sure she wants to do.<br /><br />Megan Scott is in Vegas with a group of (very bitchy) girlfriends, and they’re out partying before being bridesmaids at the wedding of one of their number the next day.  Megan has decided that she doesn’t want or need a man – she has never fallen in love with one and doesn’t think she is capable of it – instead, she intends to fulfil her desire for motherhood by a visit to the local sperm bank.<br /><br />Connor Reed is surprised – in a good way – when the gorgeous woman he’d noticed earlier as he’d walked by her table approaches him and asks him if he’ll walk her out of the bar.  Her friends have been egging her on all night, and she won’t hear the end of it if she leaves the bar alone.  It’s an odd request, but he agrees, and he and Megan end up spending the next few hours together, during which they really do ‘click’; Megan tells Connor a bit about her seeming inability to fall in love, which she puts down to the fact that her mother has been married seven times (and had boyfriends in between) and having no desire to follow the path of falling in love and being repeatedly left.  As the night progresses,  Connor becomes more and more convinced that Megan wants the same things from life that he does.  Of course, they take in more than a few more drinks along the way, which is how Megan ends up with her head stuck down the great white telephone the next morning with the hangover from hell – and discovers she’s now Mrs. Reed.<br /><br />In the spirit of ‘What happens in Vegas stays in Vegas’, she tells her new husband they made a horrendous mistake and that they should start divorce proceedings immediately – and is stunned when Connor tells her he wants their marriage to stand.  Megan can’t believe what she’s hearing, but Connor persuades her to hear him out over breakfast.  From what Megan told him the previous night, it seems she wants the same things from a relationship that he does:<br /><br /><i>“All the vital components that make a relationship successful, without any of the emotional messiness to drag it down. It’s about respect, caring and commitment. Shared goals and compatible priorities. It’s about treating a marriage like a partnership instead of some romantic fantasy. It’s about two people liking each other.”</i><br /><br />– and he’s one hundred percent there for that sort of marriage.<br /><br />Even though Megan has decided she’s probably never going to find ‘the one’, a marriage like the one Connor is suggesting sounds terribly calculating, and she’s not sure it’s what she wants for the rest of her life.  But she agrees to a three month trial – although with no sex allowed - and moves into Connor’s house.<br /><br />One of the things I liked straight away about <strong>Waking Up Married</strong> is that the ‘Oh no – we got drunk, got married and must get a divorce as quickly as possible’ trope doesn’t quite pan out that way, because while Megan and Connor did get married while drunk, Connor knew exactly what they were doing when they walked down the aisle.  The trouble is though, that I wasn’t wild about the idea that he was aware of what they were doing while Megan wasn’t; she can’t even remember saying her vows, or much of what Connor told her the previous night.  And while Connor is devastatingly handsome and extremely charming, he’s also incredibly manipulative; for the majority of the book, he’s doing his damnedest to convince Megan that what <em>he</em> wants is what <em>she</em> wants, too, which he does by being Mr. Reasonable and Mr. Unflappable, even when Megan tries everything she can think of to rile him or get him to give up – which seemed a bit mean considering she had actually agreed to give him and their marriage a chance to work out. Neither of them covers themselves in glory here, but fortunately, this stalemate isn’t allowed to continue and things start to look up – until Connor turns into an idiot not far from the end and only manages to turn things around in the last page or two.<br /><br /><strong>Waking Up Married</strong> was enjoyable - but ultimately forgettable - fluff.  I liked both protagonists, and the way Connor was so clueless as to the real state of his feelings about Megan was oddly sweet; he’s a nice blend of alpha and beta hero, a man who wants to protect and support his woman while also applauding her desire for independence.  On the downside, her being independent means less aggro for him and none of those nasty romantic luuurve cooties, so it’s not an entirely altruistic trait.  Ms. Kelly opts to give both characters a backstory that explains their reluctance to pursue love, but it’s very sketchy and could perhaps have been a little more developed; and I also have to admit that I wasn’t always comfortable with Connor’s more manipulative side.<br /><br />I can’t recommend <strong>Waking Up Married</strong> without reservations, but if you enjoy rom-coms and are looking for an afternoon quickie (!), it might hit the spot.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14845581048496453209" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3524424591" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3524424591" />
    <a title="Leticia (jerseygirl)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/118789082-leticia-jerseygirl"><img alt="Leticia (jerseygirl)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597977728p2/118789082.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3524424591?book_show_action=true">Nov 17, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Leticia (jerseygirl)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Leticia (jerseygirl)" href="/user/show/118789082-leticia-jerseygirl">Leticia (jerseygirl)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/118789082-leticia-jerseygirl?shelf=read-and-reviewed-2020">read-and-reviewed-2020</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3524424591" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14775153048515208188"><b>“Beyond reason or rationale.”</b><br/>Oh, the lies we tell ourselves to justify the things we say, do, or feel. And the walls we put up.<br/><br/><b>“Ten minutes to convince you to give me twenty. We’ll see where it goes from there.”</b><br/>I love Connor's cocky attitude. Yes, it can be a bit too much because he thinks he always gets what he wants (which I'm sure he does most of the time) and his no-strings-attached perspective pisses me off. But I do like his persistence.<br/><br/><b>“You’re a fantasy, Megan.”</b><br/>I would never say Megan and</span>
  <span id="freeText14775153048515208188" style="display:none"><b>“Beyond reason or rationale.”</b><br />Oh, the lies we tell ourselves to justify the things we say, do, or feel. And the walls we put up.<br /><br /><b>“Ten minutes to convince you to give me twenty. We’ll see where it goes from there.”</b><br />I love Connor's cocky attitude. Yes, it can be a bit too much because he thinks he always gets what he wants (which I'm sure he does most of the time) and his no-strings-attached perspective pisses me off. But I do like his persistence.<br /><br /><b>“You’re a fantasy, Megan.”</b><br />I would never say Megan and Connor could hit it off. She's looking to have a baby because she's been hurt too many times, so she's thinking she doesn't need a man for it and is ready to get artificial insemination. And then Connor comes along.<br /><br /><b>"I’m the one trying to get you mad enough to fight back. To throw down your gloves, get up in my face and prove me wrong."</b><br />None of them is looking for love. In fact, they make a point of mentioning it - with some of their concessions making me laugh out loud. And then it kind of sneaks up on them, faster for one than the other, but it's been brewing there for both of them for a while.<br /><br /><b>"Nothing halfway was enough with you."</b><br />Look, I get it. Vegas wedding. People not looking for love. You're reading this and you're thinking it's nothing you haven't read before. What makes it different for me is the writing. I suppose this could have been a disaster in the hands of so many writers, but Ms. Kelly brings it home by making the characters as great as they can be, and the happily ever after (even if expected) as sweet as she always does.<br /><br />Dislikes: her friends. They annoyed me to bits and seemed to be more about putting her down and pointing out her shortcomings than being supportive. Not cool, ladies!</span>
  <a data-text-id="14775153048515208188" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_475297432" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/475297432" />
    <a title="Danielle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4234605-danielle"><img alt="Danielle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1345088041p2/4234605.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/475297432?book_show_action=true">Dec 11, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Danielle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Danielle" href="/user/show/4234605-danielle">Danielle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4234605-danielle?shelf=please-stop-fucking">please-stop-fucking</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4234605-danielle?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4234605-danielle?shelf=netgalley-arc">netgalley-arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer475297432" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15492268319589293167">Title: Waking Up Married<br/>Author: Mira Lynn Kelly<br/>Genre: romance<br/>Series:<br/>Pages: 224 (Kindle Edition)<br/>Published: December 1, 2012<br/>Source: publishers via NetGalley<br/>Rating: 1.5 out of 5<br/><br/>Harlequin Romance conjures certain images in ones’ head, particularly if you or your mother read them in the 70s and 80s. You probably remember the red header, the schmaltzy covers, and the shamefully ludicrous plots. Harlequin has been desperately trying to put this image behind them by introducing something for every roman</span>
  <span id="freeText15492268319589293167" style="display:none">Title: Waking Up Married<br />Author: Mira Lynn Kelly<br />Genre: romance<br />Series:<br />Pages: 224 (Kindle Edition)<br />Published: December 1, 2012<br />Source: publishers via NetGalley<br />Rating: 1.5 out of 5<br /><br />Harlequin Romance conjures certain images in ones’ head, particularly if you or your mother read them in the 70s and 80s. You probably remember the red header, the schmaltzy covers, and the shamefully ludicrous plots. Harlequin has been desperately trying to put this image behind them by introducing something for every romance reader, (except the queer ones,) with 11 imprints and 21 “series”, each catering to a slightly different demographic. For a fascinating look into the industry, go on their website sometime and look at the incredibly specific requirements to be published under the Harlequin name. (<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.harlequin.com/articlepage.html?articleId=538&amp;chapter=0">http://www.harlequin.com/articlepage....</a>) <br /><br />To celebrate their newest series, Harlequin KISS, the publishers have made their first novel under this name available for free on NetGalley, Amazon and B&amp;N, and on tryharlequinkiss.com. KISS is a “NEW contemporary romance series from Harlequin” “Four stories every month of fun, flirty and sensual romances that you will love!” “Harlequin KISS stories are all about the delirium of a potential new romance – where fun-loving heroines and irresistible heroes just can’t get enough of each other.”<br /><br />In short, glossy, flirty romances, but still with a strong happily ever after. <i>Waking Up Married</i> earns every single star by embodying that ideal...for the first four chapters. <br /><br />I really liked Megan and Connor’s courtship in Vegas. It may not have been realistic, but it was smart and flirty and I felt a deeper connection between the h/h than just sex. Megan approaches Connor in a bar with a request. Pretend to leave with her to get her friends off her case. Connor agrees, but for added realism, asks her to join him for a drink first. From there, they begin a vodka soaked evening of flirting, gambling, waffles, and eventually a smoldering kiss. The next morning, they wake up, married, and while Connor remembers most of the evening, Megan’s next to a virtual stranger. She handles the situation rationally and far more calmly than I could manage. She wants to call a lawyer, but Connor still thinks they can make this work. <br /><br />And then the story utterly falls apart. Despite being madly, obviously in love with each other, Connor and Megan both deny the possibility and approach their quickie marriage as a business merger. They agree to a three month trial and if Megan’s not the perfect trophy wife Connor’s looking for, she can leave. First, I had trouble believing a successful software engineer with a plan to become a single mother would even want to be Connor’s arm candy, and secondly, I really struggled with what Connor got out of the the relationship. There was a base inequity to the relationship that the author tried to explain, but never rang true. <br /><br />Megan tries to push Connor away with bad food and a gross face mask, because she ALSO doesn’t understand why he wants her, while he pursues relentlessly, wooing her with gifts, conversation, and sex. Only after she falls for him does he take a step back and realize that maybe he’s gone too far for a business partnership. At this point he reveals himself to be an emotionally abusive sociopath, withholding all affection while Megan follows him around like a lovesick puppy. His ex conveniently turns up to narrate this and Megan, still desperately in love, flees. Even after she moves across the country, Connor keeps calling and turning up to try and convince her to come back. He refuses to take no for an answer, even after he realises that this behavior from his father is WHAT DROVE HIS MOTHER TO SUICIDE. Please pause and consider this. First he recognizes the fact that his father strung his mother along. He acknowledges that she tried to leave multiple times. He knows that her helplessness in the situation led to her death. He realizes he’s doing the same thing to Megan. HE EMBRACES IT.<br /><br />Done.<br /><br />In the end, his in-touch-with-his-emotions BFF helps Connor realizes he loves Megan too. He reads her email, because at this point, why not. He realizes she’s been approved for sperm donation. (Oh yeah, the blurb doesn’t tell you this, but the whole “contract” is about her resigning herself to being a single mom, but he’s got a pregnancy fetish and wants to impregnate her himself.) He flies to Denver, after she’s told him to leave her alone, confesses his love, says he’ll love the little bastard baby like his father never loved him, and, surprise! She didn’t go through with the sperm donation! They get back together and their HEA is that they decide to wait to have children.<br /><br />There’s nothing fun or flirty in the last 175 pages. It’s two people with tragic, traumatic pasts struggling not to let their own marriage fall apart. To twist the knife that much harder, Megan’s ex-stepfather shows up just to not remember or recognize her. Megan’s friends are flat out evil and opening mock her failed relationships. She is so starved for an emotional connection that she would have stayed with Connor through all of the neglect and loneliness, if Caro hadn’t shown up to warn her of his MO. And then she still gets sucked back in. I want to take Megan to a nice counselor to work on her self esteem and maybe get her a puppy. Connor, I just want gone.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15492268319589293167" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/605449626" />
    <a title="Andrea" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18018713-andrea"><img alt="Andrea" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1553054396p2/18018713.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/605449626?book_show_action=true">May 02, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andrea" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andrea" href="/user/show/18018713-andrea">Andrea</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer605449626" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14611886456708752962"><a href='http://booksandbindings.com/review-waking-up-married/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <b>My Review:</b>
</a><br/>I don't give out 5 hearts very easily but because it caught me off guard completely, I'm giving it the full 5 hearts it deserves. I got it for free from Amazon so I wasn't really expecting it to be this fun, quirky, and seductive. I was dreading it was going to be a bit of a heavy read and somewhat complicated but it turned out to be a predictable (in a good way) and light read, which made it way better than what I was expecting it to be. It was very cheesy and corny, which I usual</span>
  <span id="freeText14611886456708752962" style="display:none"><a href="http://booksandbindings.com/review-waking-up-married/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <b>My Review:</b>
</a><br />I don't give out 5 hearts very easily but because it caught me off guard completely, I'm giving it the full 5 hearts it deserves. I got it for free from Amazon so I wasn't really expecting it to be this fun, quirky, and seductive. I was dreading it was going to be a bit of a heavy read and somewhat complicated but it turned out to be a predictable (in a good way) and light read, which made it way better than what I was expecting it to be. It was very cheesy and corny, which I usually don't like, but surprisingly I loved reading it on this book. It had that perfect cheesiness and corniness to it.<br /><br />I went through waves of emotions from grinning like a fool to myself, squealing because of excitement, having that "uh-oh-this-is-going-to-be-a-disaster" feeling, laughing so hard forgetting there were people around me, and crying like a baby.<br /><br />Everything I'm looking for in a guy, I found in Conner.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">["All the vital components that make a relationship successful, without any of the emotional messiness to drag it down. It's about respect, caring and commitment. Shared goals and compatible priorities. It's about treating a marriage like a partnership instead of some romantic fantasy. It's about two people liking each other." <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />While reading the first few chapters of the book, I was think that sooner or later my "perfect man" fantasy of Conner will be crushed, but it wasn't.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Conner didn't release her fingers, but tightened his hold, reeling her back in. "Because you're mildly pessimistic. Now, knock it off. You don't remember, but if there's one thing we do well...it's talk. About anything." <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">["I've got you," His voice was a low rumble against her ear, the contact between them almost a kiss before he stepped back and handed her the dress. "What I want is to keep you." <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I loved Megan's character, too, and I could relate to why she hesitated a lot in trusting Conner and opening up to him. She has her reasons and she's used to being alone and independent.<br /><br />I liked another character that most probably won't even notice as much, Jeff. Oh, Jeff was funny! If I'm going to be married to someone someday, I'd love for him to have a friend like Jeff.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">["You'd been gone about thirty seconds when the 'gymnast' shows up at the table, with this whopper of a line."<br />"The gymnast? Dude!" <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">["But I have to admit that gelatinous puddle - which even Megan didn't eat, by the way - was without question the worst thing I've ever shoveled into my mouth."<br />"Dude." <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />People would find this book is cheesy, corny, predictable, too good too be true, or whatever else, but I just don't care. There are times when a girl needs to be reminded that it's okay to dream and have fantasies, no matter how far-fetched they are. This is probably the mother of all cheesy and corny lines ever, but whatever.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">["You don't remember my first proposal, but I'm hoping this one will stick. Megan, I love you. And I'm asking you to let me give you a lifetime of what you've shown me matters most. Laughter, love, late-night conversations. I'm asking you to be my wife in the most conventional, traditional and time-tested meaning of the word, for as long as we both shall live." <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Ahhhhh... melt! If you need a light, fun, quirky, and romantic read, I recommend you this book.</span>

<div id="review_488261718" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/488261718" />
    <a title="Scott-robert Shenkman" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13374703-scott-robert-shenkman"><img alt="Scott-robert Shenkman" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1349345154p2/13374703.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/488261718?book_show_action=true">Dec 28, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Scott-robert Shenkman" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Scott-robert Shenkman" href="/user/show/13374703-scott-robert-shenkman">Scott-robert Shenkman</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer488261718" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5306919234066810107">OK, so I read this comment in one of the reviews saying this was the perfect read for the ladies. Hey! Some of us guys like a nice romance once in a while. Or more than once in a while. Especially us married ones – we had to have done something right to get that ring on her finger. Of course, we’ll never admit to liking this stuff in public (and never, ever to another guy – our testosterone levels would automatically drop by 50% at least). We’ll put a cover on the paperback, and we’ll keep the K</span>
  <span id="freeText5306919234066810107" style="display:none">OK, so I read this comment in one of the reviews saying this was the perfect read for the ladies. Hey! Some of us guys like a nice romance once in a while. Or more than once in a while. Especially us married ones – we had to have done something right to get that ring on her finger. Of course, we’ll never admit to liking this stuff in public (and never, ever to another guy – our testosterone levels would automatically drop by 50% at least). We’ll put a cover on the paperback, and we’ll keep the Kindle close to our chests on the commute. If our wives get too close we’ll turn the light off on our reader and tell them we’re actually reading about the history of football or the French and Indian Wars or something manly like that. However – given the anonymity of the internet, all bets are off (that really isn’t me in my avatar; I just stole it from some romance novel cover model).<br /><br />Anyway, now that that’s off my chest, on to the review:<br /><br />I wanted light and fluffy. I expected light and fluffy. And I got light and fluffy. Until the last quarter of the book. Then it got pretty serious, because these two people have some serious history that they’re running from. Then it’s like a train wreck. But a good train wreck. Oh just read it – you’ll have fun. Look at that cover I dare – no double dare - you to tell me there won’t be an HEA here. Megan and Connor are really likeable, the plot, while predictable (and sometimes predictable is exactly what you’re looking for) is cute. I will say that Megan’s cousin and her two “best friends” are evil, and should be locked in a room together until only one is left standing. And then that one should just be left in the room.<br /><br />Speaking of the cover: Megan looks like a younger Renee Zellweger, which is totally how I see her. However, Connor looks like Jon Krasinski (maybe that is him) from “The Office”, which is not how I saw the character (I think there’s some generic perfect rugged, dark haired early-to-mid thirties guy that we’re supposed to picture when we read most of these books. Unless he’s blond) at all.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5306919234066810107" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_489947086" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/489947086" />
    <a title="..." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4299312"><img alt="..." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451675464p2/4299312.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/489947086?book_show_action=true">Dec 30, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="..." class="user" itemprop="url" name="..." href="/user/show/4299312">...</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4299312?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4299312?shelf=chick-lit">chick-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4299312?shelf=netgalley-read">netgalley-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer489947086" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14637989147314151988">I was so pleasantly surprised by this book. I honestly wasn't expecting much. And I know that's horrible to say, but it's Harlequin, and my tastes tend to be a little off from their usual style. <i>However</i>, I think the fact that this was their new KISS line had a lot to do with my overall reaction to the story, the characters and the flow.<br/><br/>First, let's talk story. This isn't a new plot. However, it's one of my favorites when done right and when fresh. I think Ms. Kelly managed both with this book, a</span>
  <span id="freeText14637989147314151988" style="display:none">I was so pleasantly surprised by this book. I honestly wasn't expecting much. And I know that's horrible to say, but it's Harlequin, and my tastes tend to be a little off from their usual style. <i>However</i>, I think the fact that this was their new KISS line had a lot to do with my overall reaction to the story, the characters and the flow.<br /><br />First, let's talk story. This isn't a new plot. However, it's one of my favorites when done right and when fresh. I think Ms. Kelly managed both with this book, and I loved the small details that made this a unique take on an old storyline.<br /><br />Now, characters. I love, love, love, love, loved Connor. Everything about him (except his idiocy). He was sweet and loyal and flirtatious and sexy and strong and funny and and and... And then there's Megan. She was basically everything I look for in a heroine, and from what I know of the KISS line, that's something that is a requirement, and I, for one, couldn't be happier. I can't stand weak, whiny heroines. I like mine with back bones and sass and smarts, and Megan had it all. <br /><br />The banter was fabulous, the flow was great, the arc wasn't rushed or trite or cliched...everything balanced nicely. I laughed and I smiled and I got that pit in my stomach when everything sort of fell apart. That's the mark of a good book for me. I mean, obviously this is a CR so you <i>know</i> there's an HEA, but <i>how</i> they were going to get there was unclear, and that made all the difference for me in going through the motions with these characters.<br /><br />If you're looking for a light-hearted, fun read with engaging and fresh characters, this is an excellent way to spend a few hours. The best part? Word on the street is this sucker is free on Amazon. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14637989147314151988" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer532531385" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9268985264403496209">Waking Up Married is a story about a couple who wakes up married in Las Vegas. Megan Scott is in Las Vegas for her cousin's wedding and meets a guy and gets drunk and wakes up married. Connor Reed is all for staying married. He wants a family but no romantic entanglements. He doesn't believe in love. Megan has major trust issues and, though she wants a baby, she doesn't want the headache of a husband. <br/><br/>It really was a cute and good story. I had to give it three stars though because I felt it drag</span>
  <span id="freeText9268985264403496209" style="display:none">Waking Up Married is a story about a couple who wakes up married in Las Vegas. Megan Scott is in Las Vegas for her cousin's wedding and meets a guy and gets drunk and wakes up married. Connor Reed is all for staying married. He wants a family but no romantic entanglements. He doesn't believe in love. Megan has major trust issues and, though she wants a baby, she doesn't want the headache of a husband. <br /><br />It really was a cute and good story. I had to give it three stars though because I felt it dragged a tad. Still, I would recommend it to contemporary romance lovers.</span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44218982-christine-kizziereads?shelf=2020-rrrc">2020-rrrc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44218982-christine-kizziereads?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3216947086" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7421461545967779312">There was too much about this that was wrong. He always wanted to make her happy with his decisions, never mind what she wanted or needed. His way was best. By the end he was so overbearing and his thoughts were so stalkerish and crazy that it was too much. I wanted to jump through the pages and punch him! </span>

<div id="review_533494953" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/533494953" />
    <a title="Anna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1406457-anna"><img alt="Anna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1357249937p2/1406457.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/533494953?book_show_action=true">Feb 11, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anna" href="/user/show/1406457-anna">Anna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1406457-anna?shelf=lovey-dovey">lovey-dovey</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer533494953" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14651379699745580056">I was conflicted about this book. I liked it a little, but the hero made me crazy. (Huh, for once I dislike HIM and not HER.) He was much too "old-school" for my taste. I kept comparing him unfavorably with Edward from "Twilight." Sparkely vampire thing aside, both characters are too good looking for words, are implausibly wealthy, and both have an inexplicable connection with our virginal (or rather conservative) heroine. Furthermore, both men disregard our leading ladies' opinions on what's be</span>
  <span id="freeText14651379699745580056" style="display:none">I was conflicted about this book. I liked it a little, but the hero made me crazy. (Huh, for once I dislike HIM and not HER.) He was much too "old-school" for my taste. I kept comparing him unfavorably with Edward from "Twilight." Sparkely vampire thing aside, both characters are too good looking for words, are implausibly wealthy, and both have an inexplicable connection with our virginal (or rather conservative) heroine. Furthermore, both men disregard our leading ladies' opinions on what's best for them, all in the name of protecting her. (Because she can't possibly know what's best for herself.) Both are manipulative and that is a major turnoff for me.<br /><br />On the other hand, Megan doesn't ALWAYS let him get away with it. In one episode, she recognized that he was trying to use sex to manipulate her and she shut him down. She even moved out and went home to a different state when she recognized that he wasn't going to give her what she wanted. I know that's old school fair, but hey, it's harder to do in real life than you'd get from most books. So points for her.<br /><br />Otherwise, there are a total of 5 other characters. 3 of them are catty, horrible harpies who tear her down, regardless of what she does. The fourth is a decent best friend to Connor and the fifth is Connor's assistant that gets a half-page of air time. I know it's only 194 pages and that doesn't lend itself to much character development apart from the main pair, but those characters were just plain awful.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14651379699745580056" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer456783262" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3771024411913246936"><i>Waking Up Married</i> is a fun, sexy read. Megan has had enough of heartbreak and disappointment in life. She has decided to take matters into her own hands. During a not so fun bachelorette party in Las Vegas, she meets Conner. The man is a walking fantasy. A whole lot of alcohol and several hours later, Megan wakes to find out she married the delicious stranger. It then comes time for the “<i>getting-to-know-your-husband date</i>.”<br/><br/>I love this. <blockquote>
  <i>“’Conner!’ <br/>‘Man, I love it when you get my name right.’ <br/>‘W</i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText3771024411913246936" style="display:none"><i>Waking Up Married</i> is a fun, sexy read. Megan has had enough of heartbreak and disappointment in life. She has decided to take matters into her own hands. During a not so fun bachelorette party in Las Vegas, she meets Conner. The man is a walking fantasy. A whole lot of alcohol and several hours later, Megan wakes to find out she married the delicious stranger. It then comes time for the “<i>getting-to-know-your-husband date</i>.”<br /><br />I love this. <blockquote>
  <i>“’Conner!’ <br />‘Man, I love it when you get my name right.’ <br />‘Wait…what?’ <br />‘Say it again for me.’”</i>
</blockquote> Conner is one determined man. He knows exactly what he wants in life, and more specifically, what he wants in a wife. For Conner, Megan is the perfect package. He can be very persuasive when he wants to be. And when it comes to his new wife, he decides enticing persuasion is the way to go. <br /> <br />This, ladies. This. <blockquote>
  <i>“It was as if he had seductive superpowers with his ability to infuse the most mundane household objects with deviant potential."</i>
</blockquote> This is a great story with more depth to the characters than I originally anticipated. It made me smile, made my heart ache, and gave me butterflies in my belly. I will definitely be checking out more books by Mira Lyn Kelly and Harlequin KISS.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/472500440" />
    <a title="Kathie (katmom)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5153260-kathie-katmom"><img alt="Kathie (katmom)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1300650721p2/5153260.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/472500440?book_show_action=true">Dec 07, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathie (katmom)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathie (katmom)" href="/user/show/5153260-kathie-katmom">Kathie (katmom)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5153260-kathie-katmom?shelf=netgalley-request">netgalley-request</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer472500440" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2337307928440492266">The title sums it up, WAKING UP MARRIED, and this is a trope that I love reading when it's done well. No worries here, as Ms. Kelly did a fabulous job of setting up the situation and then following through with the aftermath. <br/><br/>Megan's first thought upon waking up with a stranger is that she and Carter? Connor? need a divorce, like NOW.<br/><br/>But CONNOR has other ideas. He thinks that Megan is exactly what he was looking for. He wants a family, but he doesn't want love. He wants affection and fidelity. B</span>
  <span id="freeText2337307928440492266" style="display:none">The title sums it up, WAKING UP MARRIED, and this is a trope that I love reading when it's done well. No worries here, as Ms. Kelly did a fabulous job of setting up the situation and then following through with the aftermath. <br /><br />Megan's first thought upon waking up with a stranger is that she and Carter? Connor? need a divorce, like NOW.<br /><br />But CONNOR has other ideas. He thinks that Megan is exactly what he was looking for. He wants a family, but he doesn't want love. He wants affection and fidelity. But love? Well, that just brings heartache. Surely it's better to have someone that you can count on, but not someone who is going to hurt your heart.<br /><br />There was a twist later on that hurt my heart. Well done, Ms. Kelly!<br /><br />Since this is a Harlequin, we all know how it's going to end up, that's why we read these books. But what a road these two had to follow. There is sweet, hot loving...and then that dose of drama to mess with your mind and to get your heart rate up. Again, well done!<br /><br />Thank you, NetGalley and Harlequin KISS, for giving me the opportunity to read WAKING UP MARRIED by Mira Lyn Kelly.</span>
