<div id="review_655243764" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/655243764" />
    <a title="Grace Kelley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17450972-grace-kelley"><img alt="Grace Kelley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1360802894p2/17450972.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/655243764?book_show_action=true">Jun 30, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Grace Kelley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Grace Kelley" href="/user/show/17450972-grace-kelley">Grace Kelley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer655243764" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11876068097048114512"><br/>I, wow, just <i>wow</i>.<br/>In order to give a better review, I decided to organize what I hated into NOTES.<br/><br/>So I'm not going to cover the plot of the story as much as I will cover the characters, the events and just what was so unlikeable about this book.<br/><br/>Lets begin with Megan's "friends", just to get my bile about them out of the way so I don't have to bitch about them later. They are so unsupportive, unkind, catty and rude. Even <i>Gail</i>, Megan's supposed friend talks about her behind her back. They all act l</span>
  <span id="freeText11876068097048114512" style="display:none"><br />I, wow, just <i>wow</i>.<br />In order to give a better review, I decided to organize what I hated into NOTES.<br /><br />So I'm not going to cover the plot of the story as much as I will cover the characters, the events and just what was so unlikeable about this book.<br /><br />Lets begin with Megan's "friends", just to get my bile about them out of the way so I don't have to bitch about them later. They are so unsupportive, unkind, catty and rude. Even <i>Gail</i>, Megan's supposed friend talks about her behind her back. They all act like high schoolers when they are supposed to be mature women. I don't understand why Megan would hang out with them! I wouldn't like being around people who talked about me behind my back, were rude in front of me and made me miserable. Doesn't Megan have any real friends she could talk to? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Apparently not since she relies on those cows for support after she leaves her toxic relationship. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Ok, now that thats done, let me address why this plot could not work.<br /><br />The number one reason, is because  THEY DO NOT FREAKING KNOW EACH OTHER!!<br /><br />Would <u>you</u> stick with this guy in the same circumstance, a man, while attractive is completely obsessed with you staying married to him, even threatening you to make you to stay with him. <br />If you have any sanity, then the answer is a firm NO!<br /><br />I wouldn't want to be shackled to some random guy who I don't even know. And for good reason too! Connor is a nut. While he isn't lecturing Megan about why she must stay with him because they "work" (GOD, this book made me hate reading that reason, I swear if any guy I date says that to try and make me stay with him, I will punch him in the nose), he is using his body to seduce her into staying with him. <br /><br />This could count as a type of abuse. While he isn't abusive in the traditional sense of calling her names or beating her, this counts because he's using his libido and her 'fantasy maiden' innocence to attempt to control and dominate her. He even does so in the early part of the book to attempt to make her do what he wants her to do. And what is abuse but a way to gain dominance over a person. He can't even accept it when she up and leaves him, he gets drunk off his ass and tries to fly to where she lives because he has a plan thats "better than her's." I'm sorry, but when the hell do you get to decide if her plan is worse than yours. Her plan may not work for <i>you</i> but it sure as heck works for her. If you really cared about her, then you would let her go like a good boy and try to make yourself better in the head so that you could have the option of loving someone someday without destroying them or yourself.<br /><br />Now I would not have preferred Connor to have abusive tendencies at all. I would have liked to see Connor and Megan be normal people, instead of one of them having destructive control issues, and the other having deep set abandonment issues. <br /><br /><br /> I will say a little more about Connor and be careful not to repeat myself.<br />The fact that Connor is supposed to be the hero in this novel scares me. Being with an abusive partner scares me in general and waking up with a guy like this would be a living nightmare, no matter how nice he seems. What kind of message is this sending to young women in general? That its fine to be with a partner who dominates you because he'll change?<br /><br />No, there is no redemption for relationships like this unless a partner is willing to get better and overcome his or her demons to be a better person.<br /><br />But even that seems unlikely, because right before delivering his big "I Love You" speech he shouts "I'll NEVER let you go" at her. Come ON dude! That behavior is part of the reason why she left in the first place.<br /><br /><br />Onto Megan..<br /><br />She was mopey, annoying, clingy and overly dependent on toxic people. That is why she has no real friends and relies on women who have the mindsets of high-schoolers for support. That is why she did not leave the man who threatened her into staying with him until over half way through the book. And that is why, even when she realized that he had stopped giving her what she needed, she still stayed because she just is not a strong enough person to leave him. I'd hate to see how she would have been if she <i>had</i> had a child on her own. She would be too overprotective of him or her and in the end raise a wreck of a person with similar problems to her own.<br /><br />I hated when she gave in before the big reveal with Caro's return and was like, "I can accept that he will never love me again, but I'm still willing to be in this relationship", and he sees it in her demeanor and is happy. I mean, that part made me enraged. I hated that Connor felt happy even though he was damning Megan to the same loveless relationship that his mother had, different circumstances but basically the same dilemma. He feels happy even though his happiness is because of her misery. Now, I'm sure that isn't what the character was thinking consciously. I don't think Connor was sitting there being happy because Megan was sad, he was happy that she gave in to him. I hate how she had to sacrifice her happiness and joy for someone who doesn't care enough to make her happy.<br /><br /><br />The way I see life is, we have one shot at living that we are all certain of, why spend any minute of it in a depressing situation that you know you could just walk out of? Megan, before finding out that Connor moved from Caro to her in the span of 13 days was glum, when after she found out, she was packing boxes through the night and was gone by the next morning.<br /><br />While I'm laughing my head off at the sight of Connor walking into a bare house, at least she's able to make a move for herself when she needs too and escape from her own prison, no matter how gilded.<br /><br />And for those who are wondering why Caro is. She is Connors former fiancee, and was everything that Connor wanted in a wife. Someone who is able to mix within his life and have one of her own, but have emotional boundaries and not fall in love with him. Connor is someone who eventually wants to have kids someday. (I laugh at the eventual shit he'd have gotten from his children who would probably rebel against him.)<br /><br /> So Caro broke it off and left, hoping he would chase after her, because if we know him, he must have lavished all sorts of attention on her, and made her feel incredibly important. So when she heard that he was married to someone else after 13 days, she must have wanted to ruin him, get revenge and maybe save Megan from making the wrong choice. I don't think she must have hated Megan badly, just pitied her. I think all of her rage was for Connor.( What was he thinking by the way? How did he think he could explain away a thirteen day bridge between Caro and Megan. He's just nuts. He is.) <br /><br />Just getting the image of her crying in that big dining room kind of breaks my heart, she didn't deserve a guy like Connor, she deserves her own happiness. I don't think she was evil and I like the way she was handled at least. Ms. Kelly could have gone the typical route and have made her an over the top evil mega bitch, but she made her more subtle and while she still was out for revenge, it was heartbreaking and still happy for me to see her get some closure. If not revenge on Connor, at least peace for herself.<br /><br />And heres why Connor's plan will NOT work, ever.<br /><br />Children do better in normal family situations. And I'm not talking normal as in same sex couples, heterosexual couples, same race or biracial couples or any other couple that you can think of. I'm talking LOVING couples. Parents who love each other passionately and love their children fiercely. Children <b>LIKE</b> it when they see that their mommy and daddy are in love with each other, it makes them feel happy and as normal as the other children with loving mommies and daddies. Hell, even single parents do better raising children. Any parent who shows love to their children while also being a firm leader is a good one in my book. Not just this bland "we get along" shit.<br /><br />I liked it when I saw my mom and dad kiss each other, it made me feel happy and I felt secure knowing that they loved being a part of each others lives just as much as they loved being a part of mine.<br /><br />Now, when you set your child down and tell them that while mommy and daddy may <i>like</i> each other, they are not in love, what do you think your child will do. I'd probably cry. Or be sad, either way, children wouldn't like it. And they would notice. <br /><br />Children, despite what others would easily believe are not idiots, they are intelligent because they pick up on things adults would not. And they study their parents and other adults very carefully and will pick up on things that you wouldn't think they would. So when they have parents with a marriage of convenience, I'm not too sure how well it would 'work' once the rebellious teenage years hit.<br /><br /> Personally I'd hate to be a child that was not born out of love, just lust and and I would waste no time grinding that into Connor's face once I hit 15, if I was his daughter in that situation. And I'd probably rebel more and more and struggle further and further out of his grasp and put the plan he made for me (if he made a plan for his wife, he definitely made one for his children) into disarray.<br /><br />And I'd have the time of my life doing it.<br /><br />Now, I'm not saying that marriages of conveniences always fail, I'm sure that there are cases where it has worked, but I cannot see how it would work in this setting. <br /><br /><br />The only good thing about this was the one text conversation between a drunken Connor and his friend Jeff. I could picture it so clearly in my head, especially at the end. The idea of a pissed off Jeff coming in on a drunk Connor at a bar just made me laugh. And the reason why I gave it another star was because this book made me lau- No wait, I'm not rewarding it for a single funny line!<br /><br />I came into this book expecting a lighthearted comedic romance about two people falling in love with each other, despite being strangers, what I got was a story about a broken woman and a psychotic man who marry, and try to stick together despite the fact that it may be healthier for both if they divorced and saw separate therapists for several years.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11876068097048114512" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer716352480" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11545716548549625199"><a href='http://paperbackwonderland.blogspot.pt/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380238999i/681674.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><br/>Arc provided by netgalley<br/><br/>A typical romance where boy meets girl(in Vegas), the two of them get drunk, and end up married..<br/>In the morning, the guy (Connor) is pretty happy with the arrangement...the girl (Megan) who doesn't quite remember why she agreed to such a preposterous thing, is on the edge of a nervous breakdown, and wants nothing more than an annulment.<br/><br/>Here's the thing: This is well written, it has a nice flow, the characters are interesting, and basically one can read this in one si</span>
  <span id="freeText11545716548549625199" style="display:none"><a href="http://paperbackwonderland.blogspot.pt/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380238999i/681674.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br>Arc provided by netgalley<br><br>A typical romance where boy meets girl(in Vegas), the two of them get drunk, and end up married..<br>In the morning, the guy (Connor) is pretty happy with the arrangement...the girl (Megan) who doesn't quite remember why she agreed to such a preposterous thing, is on the edge of a nervous breakdown, and wants nothing more than an annulment.<br><br>Here's the thing: This is well written, it has a nice flow, the characters are interesting, and basically one can read this in one sitting. It starts out funny, the characters have a pretty good chemistry...and i could go and on, if i were a different kind of reader.<br><br>But i'm afraid i'm not the intended reading material for this kind of book.<br><br>You know when you're reading a romance that's supposed to be romantic (and leave you all smiley and happy?) but instead after awhile the only thing you see is a train wreck waiting to happen?<br>Yeah, that's me...<br><br>Relationships are hard by nature. But when an author adds some heavy emotional baggage to both the main characters, and then expects that the readers swallow all the perfect and neat ending, things can complicate themselves.<br><br>I liked that the author tried to wrote Megan as this fairly intelligent woman caught in a strange situation and deciding to make the best of it. But, i couldn't help feeling that Megan's abandonment issues were neglected in the face of Connor expectations. He calls her a liar and a coward (because she doesn't want to go through with the marriage) disrespecting what she went through. And that does she do?<br>She gives in to him and the marriage she thinks he wants..<br>But <b>Wait</b>, he has some issues as well, and it turns out that love isn't in the picture. <br>He's the kind of person capable of stop feeling whenever he wants( the expression manipulating bastard could also be used).<br><br>Of course something happens to make him see THE TRUTH..but by then, i really couldn't care.<br>Problems and fears don't disappear in a few weeks. So if you want us to believe in HEA while reading these romances, better thread lightly on the drama department...<br>Not my cup of tea...<br><br>I just wish author's would stop writing these guys as hero material. I don't care if they're rich and good looking. They're controlling, disrespectful of the other one's needs, and they don't respect boundaries!<br>If we were talking about real life, i would say: Run!<br>That, and don't marry strangers...</span>

<div id="review_468904620" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/468904620" />
    <a title="Jenn Scranton" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13142163-jenn-scranton"><img alt="Jenn Scranton" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1357149671p2/13142163.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/468904620?book_show_action=true">Dec 03, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenn Scranton" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenn Scranton" href="/user/show/13142163-jenn-scranton">Jenn Scranton</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13142163-jenn-scranton?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer468904620" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18163208698008973230">Cute :) Not quite a hot and heavy, but neither is it a mushy mushy romance. Do you know what I mean? A good classic Saturday afternoon book. I finished Waking Up Married in a afternoon and finished the last page with a smile on my face. <br/><br/>Carter? <br/>No... its Connor.<br/>Yeah, that's it.<br/><br/><br/>Hahah! Adorable romance that started out more so as an arrangement for partnership in which there would be no "love", but an easy and equal partnership between a man and a woman resulting in a family with children. It soun</span>
  <span id="freeText18163208698008973230" style="display:none">Cute :) Not quite a hot and heavy, but neither is it a mushy mushy romance. Do you know what I mean? A good classic Saturday afternoon book. I finished Waking Up Married in a afternoon and finished the last page with a smile on my face. <br><br>Carter? <br>No... its Connor.<br>Yeah, that's it.<br><br><br>Hahah! Adorable romance that started out more so as an arrangement for partnership in which there would be no "love", but an easy and equal partnership between a man and a woman resulting in a family with children. It sounds clinical. Of course it does! It was the man's perspective! Of course you can imagine, it does not stay that way. ;)<br>I mustn't give anymore details on the front for fear of ruining a cute story for everyone. <br><br>Connor: <br>A word - Work a holic. Not to mention, when he sees our girl, he sees her more like a walking uterus than a woman. Slightly disturbing... <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380399570i/773447.png" width="150" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Don't let that tough man exterior fool you. When he looks into her eyes and sees what can only be explained as love, he gets scared. As in, tail between the legs and emotionally runs away. ...Pansy <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380399570ra/773448.gif" width="150" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>However in the end he redeems himself by <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ being absolutely adorable! The fact that he thought she was pregnant, and not even by him. He wanted her, her baby, ...<i>their </i> baby. To add to that he even thought to bring a gallon of whole milk instead of champagne... <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380399570i/773449.jpg" width="150" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Cute right? It took a minute to click what and why he did, but once I got it I let out an involuntary awwwwwwwwwwwwwwwwww!<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380399570ra/773450.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>BONUS: <br>If you want to try the White Chocolate Martinis and hope to find yourself a hot billionaire looking for a bride... Here you go!<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380399570i/773451.jpg" width="150" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380399570i/773452.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('cSffCjF6NF7xfF1WeKVuZV92hVhlpgCjrcwqTUIjrQNc/MoiUIKRslXhy2wiwZGHEjyXfIkU3l4XY9tYQTQIbA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('atEyjNnm5htlaINd1nEg/Ou5VUdT72I0LxUKXtevWqVHCiekuB5D98H1FWeMFd8epvNHY79dvMmVuvtL1Lj/yg==')})
  }

Growing up in the Chicago area, she earned her degree in Fine Arts from Loyola University and met the love of her life while studying abroad in Rome, Italy… only to discover he’d been living right around the corner from her back home. Having spent her twenties working and playing in the Windy City, she’s now settled with her husband in rural Minnesota, where their four amazing children and two ridiculous dogs provide an excess of action and entertainment. When she isn’t reading, writing, or running the kids around, she loves watching the Chicago Blackhawks and action/adventure movies, blabbing with the girls, and cooking with her husband and friends.</span>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});
        } else {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('bookCover_18467968').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('bookCover_18467968').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('bookCover_18467968').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>

</li>
</ul>
